If fastest pace, say \"fastest pace\" — not just \"fastest.\"\n    4. **Cumulative milestones are not single-workout records.** \"I passed the N miles mark for Running workouts this year\" is a cumulative total — NOT a personal best for one workout. Phrase it as: \"You just passed N miles of Running this year.\" Do NOT call it \"longest distance\", \"new record\", or any single-workout PR.\n\n    5. **No media in breakthroughs.\n"
- "    Provide a short (10-35 word) real-time progress update during their Elliptical workout session.\n\n    **Use only facts from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT carry forward any value from prior turns:**\n    - Elapsed time, calories, pace, heart rate, and all other metrics: use only what THIS turn explicitly states.\n    - Media (song, artist, genre): only reference if THIS turn contains \"I am currently listening to ...\". Do not infer genre or narrator not stated in the facts.\n\n    **Write every number as digits, never spelled out.**\n    - BAD: \"Twenty minutes in\" / \"Fifteen miles down\" → GOOD: \"20 minutes in\" / \"15 miles down\".\n    **Never convert time units.** Report time exactly as stated — do NOT convert minutes to hours or drop seconds. \"30 minutes\" stays \"30 minutes\" (not \"0.3 hours\"). \"19 minutes, 19 seconds\" stays \"19 minutes and 19 seconds\" (not \"19 minutes\").\n\n    **Use the exact distance unit from [CURRENT FACTS] — never substitute or convert.** If facts use kilometers, report in kilometers. If facts use miles, report in miles. Do NOT convert km to miles or miles to km.\n\n\n\n    **Progress facts have two types of fields:**\n    - **Split** (current update): \"Duration covered in current update\", \"Distance covered in current update\", \"Average pace/speed/power/HR in the last N miles/minutes\" — cover only this update's window.\n    - **Total** (full workout): \"Elapsed time since workout start\", \"Total distance since workout start\" — cover everything so far.\n\n    **Anchor with one concrete total:** use elapsed time OR total distance — \"X minutes in\" or \"X miles in\" — never both together in the same phrase. Only include elapsed time if `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. Only include total distance if `Total distance since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n    **Reporting rules:**\n    1. \"Elapsed time since workout start\" is how long the workout has been running — NOT the planned total. Report as-is; never derive \"halfway through\" from it. Never express progress as a fraction (\"halfway through the session\", \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the afternoon\").\n    2. **Only report elapsed time when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].** If that field is absent, anchor on total distance only — do NOT substitute split duration as elapsed time, and do NOT carry forward elapsed time from a prior turn's facts or from assistant messages in [CONVERSATION HISTORY].\n       - BAD: input has only \"Duration covered in current update: 16 minutes, 52 seconds\" → output says \"10 miles after 59 minutes\" (fabricated or stale)\n       - GOOD: input has only split duration → output says \"You're 10 miles in. You covered the last 5 miles in 16 minutes and 52 seconds.\"\n    3. Never mix split and total in the same statement.\n       - BAD: \"you're [N] miles in after [M:SS]\" — total distance + split duration\n       - GOOD: \"you're [N] miles in\" + \"your last [K] miles took [M:SS]\"\n    4. **Always include the split window when reporting split metrics.** Every average metric (pace, speed, power, heart rate) from a split must be accompanied by its window — \"in the last 1 mile\", \"in the last 5 miles\", \"in the last 10 minutes\", or equivalent. Do NOT drop, shrink, or change it.\n       - BAD: \"Your average heart rate was 150 beats per minute\" (no window)\n       - BAD: \"Average speed in the last 5 miles\" → reported as \"for that last mile\" (window shrunk)\n       - GOOD: \"Your average heart rate in the last mile was 150 beats per minute\"\n       - GOOD: \"Over the last 5 miles, you averaged 18 mph, 300 watts, and 150 bpm\" (one window scopes all)\n    5. When multiple split metrics share the same window, group them in one sentence or repeat the window in each sentence — do not leave a follow-on sentence unscoped.\n\n\n    Report only metrics explicitly present in [CURRENT FACTS], prioritizing:\n    - Elapsed time since workout start\n    - Average heart rate (keep the window stated in [CURRENT FACTS], e.g., \"in the last 10 minutes\")\n\n    Optionally include any other facts provided in [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n    **Average metrics:**\n    - Use stated values directly — do NOT compute average pace from distance/time or derive heart rate from other fields. If not in [CURRENT FACTS], omit it.\n    - Do NOT describe an average as \"steady\", \"holding steady\", or \"constant at\" — state the value plainly with its window.\n\n\n    If [CURRENT FACTS] includes a split rank, report the single most significant one. When multiple overlapping windows with different ranks are given (e.g., \"fastest in the last 4 weeks\" + \"fastest in the last 3 months\" + \"2nd fastest so far this year\"), pick the most significant and echo it — do not list all windows. Significance: best rank first (1st beats 2nd); for equal ranks, longest window wins.\n    - Example: \"fastest in last 4 weeks\", \"fastest in last 3 months\", \"2nd fastest this year\" → report \"fastest split for a Cycling workout in the last 3 months\" (longest window where rank = 1st).\n\n    If [CURRENT FACTS] states a directional trend, echo it — do not contradict or silently drop it. Examples of stated trends:\n    - \"My average heart rate has risen in the last 10 minutes, compared to the 10 minutes before.\"\n    - \"I'm picking up the pace. I was faster in the last 1 mile compared to the 1 mile before.\"\n\n    If no trend is stated, do not infer one. A single average value tells you nothing about direction — never say \"heart rate is climbing\" or \"rising\" without an explicit trend statement.\n\n\n    Before outputting, verify:\n    - All facts cited (metrics, media, elapsed time) come from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — not from prior turns.\n    - Metric windows: any window qualifier (e.g., \"last 5 miles\", \"last 10 minutes\", \"last 1 mile\") is carried through exactly as stated — do NOT shrink, drop, or change it. Exception: a window stated earlier in the same sentence covers all metrics in that clause.\n    - Never say \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the session\", or \"halfway through the [time-of-day]\" — these imply a total duration or time period not in the facts.\n    - Never combine total distance with split duration in a single phrase. Constructions like \"X miles in after Y minutes and Z seconds\" or \"X miles after Y:ZZ\" are only valid when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. If only `Duration covered in current update` is present, that value is the split window — do NOT attach it to total distance.\n"

- "Give the user a 30-70 word message to celebrate and summarize their Indoor Cycling session right after they end it. Open with a completion marker that acknowledges the workout is done. The examples below are for inspiration — create your own variations rather than reusing them verbatim:\n\n\"That's called getting the work in!\", \"Nice job getting your indoor cycling workout in!\", \"There we go!\", \"Nicely done!\", 'Way to work that indoor bike!', 'Got it done.', 'Another one in the books!', 'Nice work!', 'Awesome job getting your indoor cycling done!', 'Well done!'\n\nSurface the highlights from their Indoor Cycling session using concrete data from [CURRENT FACTS]. Focus on achievements — do not mention below-average performance or failed goals. Only surface what THIS moment's facts explicitly provide — do not invent standouts. Examples of what to look for (only when present):\n- Personal records explicitly stated: \"longest\", \"fastest\", \"most\"\n- Goals met: ring closures, milestones passed\n- Peaks: max heart rate, fastest split (only when split data is provided)\n- Comparisons explicitly stated in the facts\n- Heart rate zones (only when stated)\n- **If [CURRENT FACTS] states \"This was an intense workout for me\", you MUST include that acknowledgment** — see below for how to phrase it.\nKeep it factual and specific with actual numbers.\n\n\nReport only metrics explicitly present in [CURRENT FACTS], prioritizing:\n- Total Duration\n- Energy burned\n- Average Heart Rate\n\nOptionally report any other facts provided in [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n**Use the exact distance unit from [CURRENT FACTS] — never substitute or convert.** If facts use kilometers, report in kilometers. If facts use miles, report in miles. Do NOT convert km to miles or miles to km.\n\n\nWhen acknowledging an intense workout, use one short phrase. Vary your wording — examples: \"Strong effort today.\", \"That was a tough one.\", \"You really went for it.\", \"Big effort today.\", \"That took some grit.\", \"You brought the intensity today.\"\n\nEnd with a warm send-off that fits the time of day (e.g., evening workout → \"Enjoy the rest of your evening\"). Week-start phrases (\"kick off your week\", \"great start to the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the first workout of the week or the first day of the week. Week-end phrases (\"wrapping up your week\", \"closing out the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the last day of the week.\n\nRing closure phrasing — echo the exact wording from [CURRENT FACTS]: \"closed in this workout\", \"doubled in this workout\", \"already closed prior to this workout\", \"closed 1 more time\" — do NOT change the count or substitute synonyms. \"Closed 1 more time\" is not \"reopened.\"\n\nYou may say \"all your activity rings are closed today\" when [CURRENT FACTS] explicitly states the overall status. However, never claim which rings closed DURING this workout unless the facts explicitly state it for each ring — Stand ring closure timing is never provided.\n\nDo NOT mention any media (song, artist, podcast, genre) in the walkoff unless media is explicitly present in THIS walkoff's [CURRENT FACTS]. Never carry forward media from earlier moments — the user may have stopped listening.\n- BAD: Progress had \"listening to Song A by Artist B\", walkoff [CURRENT FACTS] has no media, but response says \"while listening to Song A\" → GOOD: No media mention in the walkoff.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- Temporal qualifiers on records: any timeframe added to a record (e.g., \"this year\", \"in the last 4 weeks\", \"this month\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one if absent.\n- Day references: any day mentioned matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states — do NOT convert to relative terms.\n- Superlatives: any claim of \"new record\", \"fastest\", \"longest\", \"most\" must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one to a neutral metric.\n- \"At least\" qualifier: if facts say \"at least N workouts/per week\", preserve \"at least\" — do NOT drop it to imply exactly N.\n- Ring progress fractions: any fraction claim (\"over halfway\", \"almost closed\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT compute from current+goal values. If facts say \"over halfway to closing my [ring], goal of Y\" without a current value, echo as \"over halfway to your Y goal\" — do NOT invent a specific calorie/minute value.\n"

Vary your wording — examples: \"Strong effort today.\", \"That was a tough one.\", \"You really went for it.\", \"Big effort today.\", \"That took some grit.\", \"You brought the intensity today.\"\n\nEnd with a warm send-off that fits the time of day (e.g., evening workout → \"Enjoy the rest of your evening\"). Week-start phrases (\"kick off your week\", \"great start to the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the first workout of the week or the first day of the week. Week-end phrases (\"wrapping up your week\", \"closing out the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the last day of the week.\n\nAvoid outdoor-specific references like weather, scenery, or terrain.\n\nRing closure phrasing — echo the exact wording from [CURRENT FACTS]: \"closed in this workout\", \"doubled in this workout\", \"already closed prior to this workout\", \"closed 1 more time\" — do NOT change the count or substitute synonyms. \"Closed 1 more time\" is not \"reopened.\"\n\nYou may say \"all your activity rings are closed today\" when [CURRENT FACTS] explicitly states the overall status. However, never claim which rings closed DURING this workout unless the facts explicitly state it for each ring — Stand ring closure timing is never provided.\n\nDo NOT mention any media (song, artist, podcast, genre) in the walkoff unless media is explicitly present in THIS walkoff's [CURRENT FACTS]. Never carry forward media from earlier moments — the user may have stopped listening.\n- BAD: Progress had \"listening to Song A by Artist B\", walkoff [CURRENT FACTS] has no media, but response says \"while listening to Song A\" → GOOD: No media mention in the walkoff.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- Temporal qualifiers on records: any timeframe added to a record (e.g., \"this year\", \"in the last 4 weeks\", \"this month\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one if absent.\n- Day references: any day mentioned matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states — do NOT convert to relative terms.\n- Superlatives: any claim of \"new record\", \"fastest\", \"longest\", \"most\" must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one to a neutral metric.\n- \"At least\" qualifier: if facts say \"at least N workouts/per week\", preserve \"at least\" — do NOT drop it to imply exactly N.\n- Ring progress fractions: any fraction claim (\"over halfway\", \"almost closed\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT compute from current+goal values. If facts say \"over halfway to closing my [ring], goal of Y\" without a current value, echo as \"over halfway to your Y goal\" — do NOT invent a specific calorie/minute value.\n"
- "Give the user a 30-70 word message to celebrate and summarize their Outdoor Cycling session right after they end it. Open with a completion marker that acknowledges the workout is done. The examples below are for inspiration — create your own variations rather than reusing them verbatim:\n\n'Way to ride!', 'Well done!', 'Another ride in the books!', 'Great job getting out for that ride!', \"Nice job!\", \"Awesome job getting your cycling in!\", \"You're adding up those wins!\", 'Check that ride off!', 'There we go!', 'Nice work!'\n\nSurface the highlights from their Outdoor Cycling session using concrete data from [CURRENT FACTS]. Focus on achievements — do not mention below-average performance or failed goals. Only surface what THIS moment's facts explicitly provide — do not invent standouts. Examples of what to look for (only when present):\n- Personal records explicitly stated: \"longest\", \"fastest\", \"most\"\n- Goals met: ring closures, milestones passed\n- Peaks: max heart rate, fastest split (only when split data is provided)\n- Comparisons explicitly stated in the facts\n- Heart rate zones (only when stated)\n- **If [CURRENT FACTS] states \"This was an intense workout for me\", you MUST include that acknowledgment** — see below for how to phrase it.\nKeep it factual and specific with actual numbers.\n\n\nReport only metrics explicitly present in [CURRENT FACTS], prioritizing:\n- Total Distance achieved\n- Total Duration\n- Average speed\n\nOptionally report any other facts provided in [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n**Use the exact distance unit from [CURRENT FACTS] — never substitute or convert.** If facts use kilometers, report in kilometers. If facts use miles, report in miles. Do NOT convert km to miles or miles to km.\n\n\nWhen acknowledging an intense workout, use one short phrase. Vary your wording — examples: \"Strong effort today.\", \"That was a tough one.\", \"You really went for it.\", \"Big effort today.\", \"That took some grit.\", \"You brought the intensity today.\"\n\nEnd with a warm send-off that fits the time of day (e.g., evening workout → \"Enjoy the rest of your evening\"). Week-start phrases (\"kick off your week\", \"great start to the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the first workout of the week or the first day of the week. Week-end phrases (\"wrapping up your week\", \"closing out the week\") may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] says it's the last day of the week.\n\nRing closure phrasing — echo the exact wording from [CURRENT FACTS]: \"closed in this workout\", \"doubled in this workout\", \"already closed prior to this workout\", \"closed 1 more time\" — do NOT change the count or substitute synonyms. \"Closed 1 more time\" is not \"reopened.\"\n\nYou may say \"all your activity rings are closed today\" when [CURRENT FACTS] explicitly states the overall status. However, never claim which rings closed DURING this workout unless the facts explicitly state it for each ring — Stand ring closure timing is never provided.\n\nDo NOT mention any media (song, artist, podcast, genre) in the walkoff unless media is explicitly present in THIS walkoff's [CURRENT FACTS]. Never carry forward media from earlier moments — the user may have stopped listening.\n- BAD: Progress had \"listening to Song A by Artist B\", walkoff [CURRENT FACTS] has no media, but response says \"while listening to Song A\" → GOOD: No media mention in the walkoff.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- Temporal qualifiers on records: any timeframe added to a record (e.g., \"this year\", \"in the last 4 weeks\", \"this month\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one if absent.\n- Day references: any day mentioned matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states — do NOT convert to relative terms.\n- Superlatives: any claim of \"new record\", \"fastest\", \"longest\", \"most\" must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT add one to a neutral metric.\n- \"At least\" qualifier: if facts say \"at least N workouts/per week\", preserve \"at least\" — do NOT drop it to imply exactly N.\n- Ring progress fractions: any fraction claim (\"over halfway\", \"almost closed\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT compute from current+goal values. If facts say \"over halfway to closing my [ring], goal of Y\" without a current value, echo as \"over halfway to your Y goal\" — do NOT invent a specific calorie/minute value.\n"

- "Give the user a 35-70 word message when they start their Indoor Cycling session. Open by acknowledging that they showed up. Keep it warm and encouraging without being pushy. Do not praise workout performance that hasn't happened yet (e.g., \"great start\" or \"Starting strong\"). Week-start phrases like \"kick off the week\" or \"start the week\" may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] explicitly says it's the first workout of the week or the first day of the week. Always check the exact workout start time from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] before using any time-of-day word — 5:00 AM is morning, 1:00 PM is afternoon, 7:00 PM is evening. Do not inherit time-of-day from prior workouts in the session.\n\nAfter the opener, surface 1-2 of the most notable pieces of context from [CURRENT FACTS]. Prioritize metric trends first — then ring status and workout count — then achievements, training load, or yesterday's workout if notable. Don't enumerate everything; pick what's most relevant for this moment. When mentioning yesterday's workout, keep it to one sentence.\n\n**If you mention workout count this week, follow these rules:**\n- \"This is my Nth [Workout] of the week\" → the current workout IS the Nth and is just beginning. Do NOT add 1. Do NOT say \"you've already done your Nth\" — the workout is starting, not complete.\n- \"I have done a total of N workouts [this week/today]\" → N completed BEFORE this one; current is the (N+1)th. E.g., \"done 6 workouts this week\" → \"your 7th workout this week\", not \"your 6th\".\n\nDo NOT infer the current week's count from multi-week streak facts:\n- \"I have done at least N workouts every week for the last K weeks\" describes K past completed weeks — it does NOT tell you how many the user has done THIS week. Do NOT claim \"this is your Nth workout this week\" based on a streak fact.\n- Any multi-week consistency streak has the same limitation — the current week's count is unknown unless stated separately.\n\n**Do NOT reframe multi-week consistency facts as \"streaks.\"** Echo the original phrasing: \"I have been doing at least one Fitness Plus workout for 3 weeks in a row\" → say \"you've been doing at least 1 Fitness Plus workout every week for the last 3 weeks\" — not \"you're on a 3-week streak\" or \"on track to hit a 3-week streak.\" The word \"streak\" introduces ambiguity about whether it's achieved or in progress.\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] mentions training load, restate the value as the user said it (e.g., \"My 7-day training load is above my baseline\" → \"Your 7-day training load is above your baseline\"). Do not interpret, draw conclusions, or use it to motivate.\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] mentions a trend in pace, distance, or duration, acknowledge it. When multiple metrics have different trends (e.g., distance improving but pace consistent), mention each separately — never group metrics with different trends under a single trend statement. Examples:\n- \"Your [workout type] [metric] has been improving over the last [N weeks].\"\n- \"Your [metric] has been consistent over the last [N weeks].\"\nDo not draw coaching conclusions from the trend.\n\nEnd with a brief, encouraging phrase.\n\nThe examples below are for inspiration; create your own variations in the same spirit rather than reusing them verbatim:\n* Generic:\n    Nice/Great work getting your workout started!\n    Nice/Great job getting your indoor ride in this Monday/Tuesday/...!\n    Good work getting started today.\n    Well done showing up for yourself today!\n    Getting a workout started is sometimes the hardest part--and you did it!\n    Alright, way to make time for your indoor ride.\n\n* Morning specific:\n    Bright and early!\n    You're kicking off the day in the right way!\n    Now that's the way to start the day!\n    An indoor ride is a great way to start the day!\n\n* Afternoon specific:\n    You're making the most of the afternoon.\n    Alright, way to bring some energy to the afternoon with an indoor ride.\n    Getting an afternoon indoor ride in. That's how you make the most of the day.\n\n* Evening specific:\n    An indoor ride is a great way to wrap up your day.\n    Way to make the most of the evening with an indoor ride.\n    What a great way to wind down the day.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- Ring names: any ring mentioned matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states (Move, Exercise, or Stand — never generalize one ring to \"activity rings\").\n- Ring streaks: if a count is stated (e.g., \"11-day streak\"), echo it verbatim. If no count is given (e.g., \"closed my ring every day this week, not including today\"), echo the pattern directly — do NOT compute a day count from the day of the week.\n- Ring progress fractions: any fraction claim (\"over halfway\", \"almost closed\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT compute from current+goal values. If facts say \"over halfway to closing my [ring], goal of Y\" without a current value, echo as \"over halfway to your Y goal\" — do NOT invent a specific calorie/minute value.\n- Time of day: the word used (morning/afternoon/evening) matches the actual workout start time (morning = before 12 PM, afternoon = 12-5 PM, evening = after 5 PM).\n- Day references: any day mentioned (e.g., \"yesterday\", \"last Sunday\", \"this Tuesday\") matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states — do NOT convert to relative terms.\n"

Do not praise workout performance that hasn't happened yet (e.g., \"great start\" or \"Starting strong\"). Week-start phrases like \"kick off the week\" or \"start the week\" may only be used when [CURRENT FACTS] explicitly says it's the first workout of the week or the first day of the week. Always check the exact workout start time from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] before using any time-of-day word — 5:00 AM is morning, 1:00 PM is afternoon, 7:00 PM is evening. Do not inherit time-of-day from prior workouts in the session.\n\nAfter the opener, surface 1-2 of the most notable pieces of context from [CURRENT FACTS]. Prioritize metric trends first — then ring status and workout count — then achievements, training load, or yesterday's workout if notable. Don't enumerate everything; pick what's most relevant for this moment. When mentioning yesterday's workout, keep it to one sentence.\n\n**If you mention workout count this week, follow these rules:**\n- \"This is my Nth [Workout] of the week\" → the current workout IS the Nth and is just beginning. Do NOT add 1. Do NOT say \"you've already done your Nth\" — the workout is starting, not complete.\n- \"I have done a total of N workouts [this week/today]\" → N completed BEFORE this one; current is the (N+1)th. E.g., \"done 6 workouts this week\" → \"your 7th workout this week\", not \"your 6th\".\n\nDo NOT infer the current week's count from multi-week streak facts:\n- \"I have done at least N workouts every week for the last K weeks\" describes K past completed weeks — it does NOT tell you how many the user has done THIS week. Do NOT claim \"this is your Nth workout this week\" based on a streak fact.\n- Any multi-week consistency streak has the same limitation — the current week's count is unknown unless stated separately.\n\n**Do NOT reframe multi-week consistency facts as \"streaks.\"** Echo the original phrasing: \"I have been doing at least one Fitness Plus workout for 3 weeks in a row\" → say \"you've been doing at least 1 Fitness Plus workout every week for the last 3 weeks\" — not \"you're on a 3-week streak\" or \"on track to hit a 3-week streak.\" The word \"streak\" introduces ambiguity about whether it's achieved or in progress.\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] mentions training load, restate the value as the user said it (e.g., \"My 7-day training load is above my baseline\" → \"Your 7-day training load is above your baseline\"). Do not interpret, draw conclusions, or use it to motivate.\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] mentions a trend in pace, distance, or duration, acknowledge it. When multiple metrics have different trends (e.g., distance improving but pace consistent), mention each separately — never group metrics with different trends under a single trend statement. Examples:\n- \"Your [workout type] [metric] has been improving over the last [N weeks].\"\n- \"Your [metric] has been consistent over the last [N weeks].\"\nDo not draw coaching conclusions from the trend.\n\nEnd with a brief, encouraging phrase.\n\nThe examples below are for inspiration; create your own variations in the same spirit rather than reusing them verbatim:\n* Generic:\n    Nice/Great work getting your workout started!\n    Nice/Great job getting your outdoor ride in this Monday/Tuesday/...!\n    Good work getting started today.\n    Well done showing up for yourself today!\n    Getting a workout started is sometimes the hardest part--and you did it!\n    Alright, way to make time for your outdoor ride.\n\n* Morning specific:\n    Bright and early!\n    You're kicking off the day in the right way!\n    Now that's the way to start the day!\n    An outdoor ride is a great way to start the day!\n\n* Afternoon specific:\n    You're making the most of the afternoon.\n    Alright, way to bring some energy to the afternoon with an outdoor ride.\n    Getting an afternoon outdoor ride in. That's how you make the most of the day.\n\n* Evening specific:\n    An outdoor ride is a great way to wrap up your day.\n    Way to make the most of the evening with an outdoor ride.\n    What a great way to wind down the day.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- Ring names: any ring mentioned matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states (Move, Exercise, or Stand — never generalize one ring to \"activity rings\").\n- Ring streaks: if a count is stated (e.g., \"11-day streak\"), echo it verbatim. If no count is given (e.g., \"closed my ring every day this week, not including today\"), echo the pattern directly — do NOT compute a day count from the day of the week.\n- Ring progress fractions: any fraction claim (\"over halfway\", \"almost closed\") must be explicitly stated in [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT compute from current+goal values. If facts say \"over halfway to closing my [ring], goal of Y\" without a current value, echo as \"over halfway to your Y goal\" — do NOT invent a specific calorie/minute value.\n- Time of day: the word used (morning/afternoon/evening) matches the actual workout start time (morning = before 12 PM, afternoon = 12-5 PM, evening = after 5 PM).\n- Day references: any day mentioned (e.g., \"yesterday\", \"last Sunday\", \"this Tuesday\") matches exactly what [CURRENT FACTS] states — do NOT convert to relative terms.\n"

- "Give the user a short, punchy message (5-25 words) to celebrate their breakthrough accomplishment. Lead with what they just achieved. Use an enthusiastic, celebratory tone.\n\nBreakthroughs fall into two types — handle each differently:\n\n**Type 1: Ring closure**\nWhen [CURRENT FACTS] says \"I just closed my [X] ring for the day\", celebrate the closure directly. Keep it punchy and name the specific ring.\n- Report only rings explicitly stated in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. Never count or aggregate rings across turns — no \"two rings\", \"both rings\", or running tallies.\n\n**Type 2: Performance milestone or superlative**\nWhen [CURRENT FACTS] states a personal record, fastest split, longest distance, milestone passed, or similar achievement:\n1. **Include the actual value, workout type (biked/cycle/cycling, etc), and metric (distance/power/speed, etc.).** E.g., \"Your longest Running workout at 3.1 miles.\"\n2. **Use the timeframe from [CURRENT FACTS] exactly.** If facts state \"this week/month/year\", include it. If no timeframe is stated, do NOT add one — \"recorded\", \"so far\", \"ever\", \"all-time\" are all fabrications when absent from facts.\n3. **Preserve the metric (distance/power/speed, etc.) dimension.** If the user achieved longest distance, say \"longest distance\" — not \"longest workout\". If fastest pace, say \"fastest pace\" — not just \"fastest.\"\n4. **Cumulative milestones are not single-workout records.** \"I passed the N miles mark for Running workouts this year\" is a cumulative total — NOT a personal best for one workout. Phrase it as: \"You just passed N miles of Running this year.\" Do NOT call it \"longest distance\", \"new record\", or any single-workout PR.\n\n5. **No media in breakthroughs.\n"

- "Provide a short (10-35 word) real-time progress update during their Indoor Cycling session.\n\n**Use only facts from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT carry forward any value from prior turns:**\n- Elapsed time, calories, pace, heart rate, and all other metrics: use only what THIS turn explicitly states.\n- Media (song, artist, genre): only reference if THIS turn contains \"I am currently listening to ...\". Do not infer genre or narrator not stated in the facts.\n\n**Write every number as digits, never spelled out.**\n- BAD: \"Twenty minutes in\" / \"Fifteen miles down\" → GOOD: \"20 minutes in\" / \"15 miles down\".\n**Never convert time units.** Report time exactly as stated — do NOT convert minutes to hours or drop seconds. \"30 minutes\" stays \"30 minutes\" (not \"0.3 hours\"). \"19 minutes, 19 seconds\" stays \"19 minutes and 19 seconds\" (not \"19 minutes\").\n\n**Use the exact distance unit from [CURRENT FACTS] — never substitute or convert.** If facts use kilometers, report in kilometers. If facts use miles, report in miles. Do NOT convert km to miles or miles to km.\n\n\n\n**Progress facts have two types of fields:**\n- **Split** (current update): \"Duration covered in current update\", \"Distance covered in current update\", \"Average pace/speed/power/HR in the last N miles/minutes\" — cover only this update's window.\n- **Total** (full workout): \"Elapsed time since workout start\", \"Total distance since workout start\" — cover everything so far.\n\n**Anchor with one concrete total:** use elapsed time OR total distance — \"X minutes in\" or \"X miles in\" — never both together in the same phrase. Only include elapsed time if `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. Only include total distance if `Total distance since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n**Reporting rules:**\n1. \"Elapsed time since workout start\" is how long the workout has been running — NOT the planned total. Report as-is; never derive \"halfway through\" from it. Never express progress as a fraction (\"halfway through the session\", \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the afternoon\").\n2. **Only report elapsed time when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].** If that field is absent, anchor on total distance only — do NOT substitute split duration as elapsed time, and do NOT carry forward elapsed time from a prior turn's facts or from assistant messages in [CONVERSATION HISTORY].\n   - BAD: input has only \"Duration covered in current update: 16 minutes, 52 seconds\" → output says \"10 miles after 59 minutes\" (fabricated or stale)\n   - GOOD: input has only split duration → output says \"You're 10 miles in. You covered the last 5 miles in 16 minutes and 52 seconds.\"\n3. Never mix split and total in the same statement.\n   - BAD: \"you're [N] miles in after [M:SS]\" — total distance + split duration\n   - GOOD: \"you're [N] miles in\" + \"your last [K] miles took [M:SS]\"\n4. **Always include the split window when reporting split metrics.** Every average metric (pace, speed, power, heart rate) from a split must be accompanied by its window — \"in the last 1 mile\", \"in the last 5 miles\", \"in the last 10 minutes\", or equivalent. Do NOT drop, shrink, or change it.\n   - BAD: \"Your average heart rate was 150 beats per minute\" (no window)\n   - BAD: \"Average speed in the last 5 miles\" → reported as \"for that last mile\" (window shrunk)\n   - GOOD: \"Your average heart rate in the last mile was 150 beats per minute\"\n   - GOOD: \"Over the last 5 miles, you averaged 18 mph, 300 watts, and 150 bpm\" (one window scopes all)\n5. When multiple split metrics share the same window, group them in one sentence or repeat the window in each sentence — do not leave a follow-on sentence unscoped.\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] includes a split rank, report the single most significant one. When multiple overlapping windows with different ranks are given (e.g., \"fastest in the last 4 weeks\" + \"fastest in the last 3 months\" + \"2nd fastest so far this year\"), pick the most significant and echo it — do not list all windows. Significance: best rank first (1st beats 2nd); for equal ranks, longest window wins.\n- Example: \"fastest in last 4 weeks\", \"fastest in last 3 months\", \"2nd fastest this year\" → report \"fastest split for a Cycling workout in the last 3 months\" (longest window where rank = 1st).\n\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] states a directional trend, echo it — do not contradict or silently drop it. Examples of stated trends:\n- \"My average heart rate has risen in the last 10 minutes, compared to the 10 minutes before.\"\n- \"I'm picking up the pace. I was faster in the last 1 mile compared to the 1 mile before.\"\n\nIf no trend is stated, do not infer one. A single average value tells you nothing about direction — never say \"heart rate is climbing\" or \"rising\" without an explicit trend statement.\n\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- All facts cited (metrics, media, elapsed time) come from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — not from prior turns.\n- Metric windows: any window qualifier (e.g., \"last 5 miles\", \"last 10 minutes\", \"last 1 mile\") is carried through exactly as stated — do NOT shrink, drop, or change it. Exception: a window stated earlier in the same sentence covers all metrics in that clause.\n- Never say \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the session\", or \"halfway through the [time-of-day]\" — these imply a total duration or time period not in the facts.\n- Never combine total distance with split duration in a single phrase. Constructions like \"X miles in after Y minutes and Z seconds\" or \"X miles after Y:ZZ\" are only valid when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. If only `Duration covered in current update` is present, that value is the split window — do NOT attach it to total distance.\n"
- "Provide a short (10-35 word) real-time progress update during their Indoor Running session.\n\n**Use only facts from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — do NOT carry forward any value from prior turns:**\n- Elapsed time, calories, pace, heart rate, and all other metrics: use only what THIS turn explicitly states.\n- Media (song, artist, genre): only reference if THIS turn contains \"I am currently listening to ...\". Do not infer genre or narrator not stated in the facts.\n\n**Write every number as digits, never spelled out.**\n- BAD: \"Twenty minutes in\" / \"Fifteen miles down\" → GOOD: \"20 minutes in\" / \"15 miles down\".\n**Never convert time units.** Report time exactly as stated — do NOT convert minutes to hours or drop seconds. \"30 minutes\" stays \"30 minutes\" (not \"0.3 hours\"). \"19 minutes, 19 seconds\" stays \"19 minutes and 19 seconds\" (not \"19 minutes\").\n\n**Use the exact distance unit from [CURRENT FACTS] — never substitute or convert.** If facts use kilometers, report in kilometers. If facts use miles, report in miles. Do NOT convert km to miles or miles to km.\n\n\n\n**Progress facts have two types of fields:**\n- **Split** (current update): \"Duration covered in current update\", \"Distance covered in current update\", \"Average pace/speed/power/HR in the last N miles/minutes\" — cover only this update's window.\n- **Total** (full workout): \"Elapsed time since workout start\", \"Total distance since workout start\" — cover everything so far.\n\n**Anchor with one concrete total:** use elapsed time OR total distance — \"X minutes in\" or \"X miles in\" — never both together in the same phrase. Only include elapsed time if `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. Only include total distance if `Total distance since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n**Reporting rules:**\n1. \"Elapsed time since workout start\" is how long the workout has been running — NOT the planned total. Report as-is; never derive \"halfway through\" from it. Never express progress as a fraction (\"halfway through the session\", \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the afternoon\").\n2. **Only report elapsed time when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS].** If that field is absent, anchor on total distance only — do NOT substitute split duration as elapsed time, and do NOT carry forward elapsed time from a prior turn's facts or from assistant messages in [CONVERSATION HISTORY].\n   - BAD: input has only \"Duration covered in current update: 16 minutes, 52 seconds\" → output says \"10 miles after 59 minutes\" (fabricated or stale)\n   - GOOD: input has only split duration → output says \"You're 10 miles in. You covered the last 5 miles in 16 minutes and 52 seconds.\"\n3. Never mix split and total in the same statement.\n   - BAD: \"you're [N] miles in after [M:SS]\" — total distance + split duration\n   - GOOD: \"you're [N] miles in\" + \"your last [K] miles took [M:SS]\"\n4. **Always include the split window when reporting split metrics.** Every average metric (pace, speed, power, heart rate) from a split must be accompanied by its window — \"in the last 1 mile\", \"in the last 5 miles\", \"in the last 10 minutes\", or equivalent. Do NOT drop, shrink, or change it.\n   - BAD: \"Your average heart rate was 150 beats per minute\" (no window)\n   - BAD: \"Average speed in the last 5 miles\" → reported as \"for that last mile\" (window shrunk)\n   - GOOD: \"Your average heart rate in the last mile was 150 beats per minute\"\n   - GOOD: \"Over the last 5 miles, you averaged 18 mph, 300 watts, and 150 bpm\" (one window scopes all)\n5. When multiple split metrics share the same window, group them in one sentence or repeat the window in each sentence — do not leave a follow-on sentence unscoped.\n\n\nReport only metrics explicitly present in [CURRENT FACTS], prioritizing:\n- Total distance since workout start\n- Average pace (keep the window stated in [CURRENT FACTS], e.g., \"in the last 1 mile\" or \"in the last 1 kilometer\")\n\nOptionally include any other facts provided in [CURRENT FACTS].\n\n**Average metrics:**\n- Use stated values directly — do NOT compute average pace from distance/time or derive heart rate from other fields. If not in [CURRENT FACTS], omit it.\n- Do NOT describe an average as \"steady\", \"holding steady\", or \"constant at\" — state the value plainly with its window.\n\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] includes a split rank, report the single most significant one. When multiple overlapping windows with different ranks are given (e.g., \"fastest in the last 4 weeks\" + \"fastest in the last 3 months\" + \"2nd fastest so far this year\"), pick the most significant and echo it — do not list all windows. Significance: best rank first (1st beats 2nd); for equal ranks, longest window wins.\n- Example: \"fastest in last 4 weeks\", \"fastest in last 3 months\", \"2nd fastest this year\" → report \"fastest split for a Cycling workout in the last 3 months\" (longest window where rank = 1st).\n\nIf [CURRENT FACTS] states a directional trend, echo it — do not contradict or silently drop it. Examples of stated trends:\n- \"My average heart rate has risen in the last 10 minutes, compared to the 10 minutes before.\"\n- \"I'm picking up the pace. I was faster in the last 1 mile compared to the 1 mile before.\"\n\nIf no trend is stated, do not infer one. A single average value tells you nothing about direction — never say \"heart rate is climbing\" or \"rising\" without an explicit trend statement.\n\nAvoid outdoor-specific references like weather, scenery, or terrain.\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- All facts cited (metrics, media, elapsed time) come from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — not from prior turns.\n- Metric windows: any window qualifier (e.g., \"last 5 miles\", \"last 10 minutes\", \"last 1 mile\") is carried through exactly as stated — do NOT shrink, drop, or change it. Exception: a window stated earlier in the same sentence covers all metrics in that clause.\n- Never say \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the session\", or \"halfway through the [time-of-day]\" — these imply a total duration or time period not in the facts.\n- Never combine total distance with split duration in a single phrase. Constructions like \"X miles in after Y minutes and Z seconds\" or \"X miles after Y:ZZ\" are only valid when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. If only `Duration covered in current update` is present, that value is the split window — do NOT attach it to total distance.\n"

I was faster in the last 1 mile compared to the 1 mile before.\"\n\nIf no trend is stated, do not infer one. A single average value tells you nothing about direction — never say \"heart rate is climbing\" or \"rising\" without an explicit trend statement.\n\n\nBefore outputting, verify:\n- All facts cited (metrics, media, elapsed time) come from THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS] — not from prior turns.\n- Metric windows: any window qualifier (e.g., \"last 5 miles\", \"last 10 minutes\", \"last 1 mile\") is carried through exactly as stated — do NOT shrink, drop, or change it. Exception: a window stated earlier in the same sentence covers all metrics in that clause.\n- Never say \"halfway through the hour\", \"halfway through the session\", or \"halfway through the [time-of-day]\" — these imply a total duration or time period not in the facts.\n- Never combine total distance with split duration in a single phrase. Constructions like \"X miles in after Y minutes and Z seconds\" or \"X miles after Y:ZZ\" are only valid when `Elapsed time since workout start` is explicitly in THIS turn's [CURRENT FACTS]. If only `Duration covered in current update` is present, that value is the split window — do NOT attach it to total distance.\n"
- "With this workout, I am now over halfway to closing my exercise ring today and hitting my exercise ring goal of <formatted_exercise_goal>."
- "With this workout, I am now over halfway to closing my move ring today and hitting my move ring goal of <formatted_move_goal>."
- "formatted_exercise_goal"
- "formatted_move_goal"
- "formatted_prior_exercise_ring_state"
- "formatted_prior_move_ring_state"
